## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt in a chemical reaction, where the rate law relates the reaction rate to the current concentration A and possibly time t. Classical kinetics provides various rate law forms from elementary and complex reaction mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combination of first and second order)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics / saturation kinetics)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface catalysis with competitive adsorption)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent rate coefficient)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 (multiple simultaneous pathways)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Fractal kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A (time-dependent rate in heterogeneous media)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Concentration power-law dependence → A**n where n is the reaction order, reflecting molecularity of elementary steps
- Rational functions of concentration → Indicate pre-equilibrium or steady-state intermediate species that have been algebraically eliminated
- Product of concentration and (capacity - concentration) → Autocatalytic or reversible reactions approaching equilibrium: A*(c-A)
- Time-dependent prefactor multiplying concentration terms → Suggests catalyst deactivation, photolytic intensity changes, or diffusion-limited kinetics in heterogeneous systems
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A → Parallel competing reaction pathways with different molecularities
- Denominator polynomial in A → Enzyme or surface catalysis where binding/adsorption creates saturation effects from quasi-steady-state approximation
- Square root or fractional power of A → Dissociative adsorption on surfaces or radical chain mechanisms where intermediates scale as sqrt(A)
- Negative constant term added to rate expression → Back-reaction or product inhibition in reversible reactions near equilibrium
